The secret of Japanese baseball education lies in the "Koshien" system,  a biannual tournament involving the entire nation, in which all 47 prefectures of Japan compete against each other in a national high school baseball tournament.  All players are required to go to this tournament to learn basic baseball training and tactics, and to experience the big stage of a sudden-death tournament, which is a grueling training experience for character development, mental strength, technique, and physical ability  in their teenage years.  This system is unique in Japan.  This is what produced Otani and Ichiro.  USA does not recognize the "Koshien" system.

â€œWhy is the Japanese team so strong?" No, this is better phrased, for the sake of simplicity, as "Why are players from the Japanese baseball system so strong?" Can we say that it is because the Japanese team this time has strong members? If so, it would be a transient thing produced by coincidence.  However, the reason â€œwhy Japanese baseball is strongâ€ in international tournaments is not because they have strong members and excellent coaches. It is because they are â€œnot players who grew up learning baseballâ€ in the United States. They were â€œeducated in Japan's unique system of baseball educationâ€, and the best of them were selected to become Japanese professionals, and some of them have made it to the majors in the U.S.A., the Japanese baseball players are not American-bred. Needless to say, baseball is a sport born in the United States, and each country in this tournament has its own major leaguers.  The Japanese team, however, is made up of players who have been educated and nurtured in the Japanese baseball system, including coaches and managers. The strength of the Japanese baseball team is that it is a group of players from â€œthe Japanese baseball education systemâ€, not players educated in the U.S. This is the biggest characteristic and difference between the Japanese team and the U.S. team.ã€€  This is not only the difference from USA teams, but also from Chinese, Korean, and Taiwanese teams in Asia. Unless Americans accurately recognize this, they will not know the strength of the Japanese team, nor will they be able to develop countermeasures. â€œWhy do players like Ichiro and Otani emerge from Japanese baseball?â€ â€œWhy are Japanese pitchers and fielders so precise and well mastered in their defense?â€ â€œWhy are Japanese players able to play calmly on the big stage and in a pinch? â€œ This is a big difference from American baseball, which is the result of â€œthe difference in educationâ€ they have received since their childhood and school days.  It cannot be dismissed as a cultural difference from Japan. The difference in the educational environment during their school days and the difference in the content of baseball education are the secrets of the source of the strength of Japanese baseball. Americans are surprised at the results of the games because they don't know this and don't want to know it.  There are causes and reasons for all facts.

all complete overreactions aside, this tournament has been very good. I had been hyping this tournament since it was announced, but when the rosters were announced i was actually fairly disappointed.  For starters, as a fan of pitching more than hitting, the fact that 20 of the top 25/30 starters in the world were missing wasnt the best. On top of that we were missing Fernando Tatis , Alejandro Kirk,Aaron Judge and Cuban stars (Yordan Alvarez, Abreu, Chapman, )  for various reasons, and the sheer amount of nation flip-flopping, whether it be marcus stroman, or a lot of players on the mexican , israel, italy squads, it just felt a little lackluster.    However i suppose the fact that most of the star hitters were participating and the star pitchers werent works out quite nicely for an entertaining baseball game.  It had just the right amount of star pitchers sprinkled in as well. There have also been like 3 or 4 extremely good games that had elimination on the line so far.  Hopefully the final does not disaapoint

Both these teams and this game proved three things.  1) Teams baseball (take good at bats with a solid approach, hit the other way, pass the bat to the next guy in the lineup and play solid fundamental baseball in the field) is still winning baseball at any level,  2) The changes to the MLB Official Rules of Baseball for 2023 were unnecessary to produce entertaining, engaging and watchable baseball, and 3) The World Baseball Classic matters a whole lot to a whole lot of people around the world.    We fans in the US could learn a lot from those two passionate, knowledgeable and engaged fan bases from Mexico and Japan.  And we could learn a lot from the many other fans and players from around the world who just appreciate and play the game rather than copping out and changing the rules to produce something that looks more like an RL version of MLB the Show.    Both these teams were so hard to beat and they threw haymakers at each other until the final bell.  When two teams are playing team baseball like this, instead of some grotesque form of modified home run derby, baseball is a beautiful game to watch.  Throw out the analytics, throw out the rules changes and just play the game.    It was a shame that this wasn't the championship game and a shame that one of these teams had to lose.  Huge respect to both teams for producing the best game of the tournament with such high level baseball and showing the world how entertaining baseball really is.

According to ESPN Stats & Info, Samurai Japan walks it off against Mexico to win 6-5 and advance to their 3rd World Baseball Classic Final. This is Japan's 1st walk-off WBC win and the 2nd walk-off win in the semifinals or later in WBC history, along with Puerto Rico in the 2017 Semis over the Netherlands. Japan is now 6-0 at this year's WBC, the only remaining unbeaten team. The only team to finish the WBC undefeated is the Dominican Republic in 2013 (8-0).
